// This is a low-overhead replacement for std::visit. It generates a series of
179
// if/else branches that figure out what is the type of the currently held
180
// value in the variant and then they call F (with return type R) which is
181
// specialized for that type.
182
//
183
// The return type must be explicitly specified.
184
//
185
// TODO: get rid of the explicitly specified return type the compiler cannot
186
// deduce the return type more metaprogramming required...
187
template <typename R, typename F, typename... Types>
188
2.13k
__attribute__((always_inline)) R visit(F &&f, std::variant<Types...> &v) {
189
2.13k
  return visit_impl<R, F, std::variant<Types...>, Types...>(std::forward<F>(f),
190
2.13k
                                                            v);
191
2.13k
}

template <typename R, typename FUN, typename IntegerVariant>
333
__attribute__((always_inline)) R visitSafeInt(FUN &&fun, IntegerVariant arg) {
334
  return detail::visit<R>([&fun](auto &i) { return fun(i); }, arg);
335
}
336
337
template <typename R, typename FUN, typename IntegerVariant, typename... ARGS>
338
__attribute__((always_inline)) R visitSafeInt(FUN &&fun, IntegerVariant arg,
339
                                              ARGS &... rest) {
340
  return detail::visit<R>([&fun, &rest...](auto &i) { return fun(i, rest...); },
341
                          arg);
342
}

}
